<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cities and large towns are connected with <a href="/wiki/Asphalt" title="Asphalt">asphalt</a>-paved roads, while smaller towns are often connected by dirt roads, which may require a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Four-wheel-drive" title="Four-wheel-drive">four-wheel-drive</a> vehicle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-andesmap_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-andesmap-36">[36]</a></sup>
</p><p>The rough terrain has historically put the costs of building <a href="/wiki/Highway" title="Highway">highways</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Railroad" title="Railroad">railroads</a> that cross the Andes out of reach of most neighboring countries, even with modern <a href="/wiki/Civil_engineering" title="Civil engineering">civil engineering</a> practices. For example, the main crossover of the Andes between Argentina and Chile is still accomplished through the <a href="/wiki/Paso_Internacional_Los_Libertadores" title="Paso Internacional Los Libertadores">Paso Internacional Los Libertadores</a>. Only recently the ends of some highways that came rather close to one another from the east and the west have been connected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> Much of the transportation of passengers is done via aircraft.
</p><p>However, there is one railroad that connects Chile with Peru via the Andes, and there are others that make the same connection via southern Bolivia. See railroad maps of that region.
</p><p>There are multiple highways in Bolivia that cross the Andes. Some of these were built during a <a href="/wiki/Chaco_War" title="Chaco War">period of war</a> between Bolivia and <a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a>, in order to transport Bolivian troops and their supplies to the war front in the lowlands of southeastern Bolivia and western Paraguay.
</p><p>For decades, Chile claimed ownership of land on the eastern side of the Andes. However, these claims were given up in about 1870 during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Pacific" title="War of the Pacific">War of the Pacific</a> between Chile, the allied Bolivia and Peru, in a diplomatic deal to keep Peru out of the war. The <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Army" title="Chilean Army">Chilean Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Navy" title="Chilean Navy">Chilean Navy</a> defeated the combined forces of Bolivia and Peru, and Chile took over Bolivia's only province on the Pacific Coast, some land from Peru that was returned to Peru decades later. Bolivia has been a completely <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landlocked" title="Landlocked">landlocked</a> country ever since. It mostly uses <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seaport" title="Seaport">seaports</a> in eastern Argentina and <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a> for international trade because its diplomatic relations with Chile have been suspended since 1978.
</p><p>Because of the tortuous terrain in places, villages and towns in the mountains—to which travel via <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motorized_vehicle" title="Motorized vehicle">motorized vehicles</a> is of little use—are still located in the high Andes of Chile, Bolivia, Peru, and <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>. Locally, the relatives of the <a href="/wiki/Camel" title="Camel">camel</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Llama" title="Llama">llama</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Alpaca" title="Alpaca">alpaca</a> continue to carry out important uses as pack animals, but this use has generally diminished in modern times. <a href="/wiki/Donkey" title="Donkey">Donkeys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mule" title="Mule">mules</a>, and horses are also useful.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Peruvianterracefarmers.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Peruvianterracefarmers.jpg/220px-Peruvianterracefarmers.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Peruvianterracefarmers.jpg/330px-Peruvianterracefarmers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Peruvianterracefarmers.jpg/440px-Peruvianterracefarmers.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Peruvianterracefarmers.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Peruvian farmers sowing maize and beans</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Andean_Agriculture" title="Andean Agriculture">Andean Agriculture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Incan_agriculture" title="Incan agriculture">Incan agriculture</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Vertical_archipelago" title="Vertical archipelago">Vertical archipelago</a></div>
<p>The ancient peoples of the Andes such as the Incas have practiced <a href="/wiki/Irrigation" title="Irrigation">irrigation</a> techniques for over 6,000 years. Because of the mountain slopes, <a href="/wiki/And%C3%A9n" title="Andén">terracing</a> has been a common practice. Terracing, however, was only extensively employed after Incan imperial expansions to fuel their expanding realm. The <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">potato</a> holds a very important role as an internally consumed staple crop. <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">Maize</a> was also an important crop for these people, and was used for the production of <a href="/wiki/Chicha" title="Chicha">chicha</a>, important to Andean native people. Currently, <a href="/wiki/Tobacco" title="Tobacco">tobacco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a> are the main export crops. <a href="/wiki/Coca" title="Coca">Coca</a>, despite eradication programmes in some countries, remains an important crop for legal local use in a mildly stimulating <a href="/wiki/Herbal_tea" title="Herbal tea">herbal tea</a>, and, both controversially and illegally, for the production of <a href="/wiki/Cocaine" title="Cocaine">cocaine</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Irrigation">Irrigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Irrigation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Women_irrigators_in_the_Andes.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="456" decoding="async" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Women_irrigators_in_the_Andes.jpg/220px-Women_irrigators_in_the_Andes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Women_irrigators_in_the_Andes.jpg/330px-Women_irrigators_in_the_Andes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Women_irrigators_in_the_Andes.jpg/440px-Women_irrigators_in_the_Andes.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Women_irrigators_in_the_Andes.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Irrigating land in the Peruvian Andes</div></div></div>
<p>In unirrigated land, <a href="/wiki/Pasture" title="Pasture">pasture</a> is the most common type of land use. In the rainy season (summer), part of the rangeland is used for cropping (mainly potatoes, barley, broad beans and wheat).
</p><p>Irrigation is helpful in advancing the sowing data of the summer crops which guarantees an early yield in the period of food shortage. Also, by early sowing, maize can be cultivated higher up in the mountains (up to 3,800 m (12,500 ft)). In addition, it makes cropping in the dry season (winter) possible and allows the cultivation of frost-resistant vegetable crops like <a href="/wiki/Onion" title="Onion">onion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carrot" title="Carrot">carrot</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mining">Mining</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Mining">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Huasos_Maulinos_-_Rugendas.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2717" data-file-width="3200" decoding="async" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Huasos_Maulinos_-_Rugendas.jpg/220px-Huasos_Maulinos_-_Rugendas.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Huasos_Maulinos_-_Rugendas.jpg/330px-Huasos_Maulinos_-_Rugendas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Huasos_Maulinos_-_Rugendas.jpg/440px-Huasos_Maulinos_-_Rugendas.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Huasos_Maulinos_-_Rugendas.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chilean <a href="/wiki/Huaso" title="Huaso">huasos</a>, 19th century</div></div></div>
<p>The Andes rose to fame for their mineral wealth during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish conquest of South America</a>. Although Andean Amerindian peoples crafted ceremonial jewelry of gold and other metals, the <a href="/wiki/Mineralization_(geology)" title="Mineralization (geology)">mineralizations</a> of the Andes were first mined on a large scale after the Spanish arrival. <a href="/wiki/Potos%C3%AD" title="Potosí">Potosí</a> in present-day <a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cerro_de_Pasco" title="Cerro de Pasco">Cerro de Pasco</a> in Peru were among the principal mines of the Spanish Empire in the New World. <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_de_la_Plata" title="Río de la Plata">Río de la Plata</a> and <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> derive their names from the silver of Potosí.
</p><p>Currently, mining in the Andes of <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> places these countries as the first and second major producers of <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a> in the world. <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> also contains the 4th largest goldmine in the world: the <a href="/wiki/Yanacocha" title="Yanacocha">Yanacocha</a>. The Bolivian Andes produce principally <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a> although historically silver mining had a huge impact on the <a href="/wiki/Price_revolution" title="Price revolution">economy</a> of 17th century Europe.
</p><p>There is a long history of mining in the Andes, from the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Silver" title="Silver">silver</a> <a href="/wiki/Mining" title="Mining">mines</a> in <a href="/wiki/Potos%C3%AD" title="Potosí">Potosí</a> in the 16th century to the vast current <a href="/wiki/Porphyry_copper_deposit" title="Porphyry copper deposit">porphyry copper deposits</a> of <a href="/wiki/Chuquicamata" title="Chuquicamata">Chuquicamata</a> and <a href="/wiki/Escondida" title="Escondida">Escondida</a> in Chile and <a href="/wiki/Toquepala_mine" title="Toquepala mine">Toquepala</a> in Peru. Other metals including iron, gold, and tin in addition to non-metallic resources are important.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Peaks">Peaks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Peaks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mountains_in_the_Andes" title="List of mountains in the Andes">List of mountains in the Andes</a></div>
<p>This list contains some of the major peaks in the Andes mountain range. The highest peak is Aconcagua of Argentina (see below).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Argentina">Argentina</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andes&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Argentina">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aconcagua_(aerial).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1712" data-file-width="2288" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Aconcagua_%28aerial%29.jpg/220px-Aconcagua_%28aerial%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Aconcagua_%28aerial%29.jpg/330px-Aconcagua_%28aerial%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Aconcagua_%28aerial%29.jpg/440px-Aconcagua_%28aerial%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aconcagua_(aerial).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Aconcagua" title="Aconcagua">Aconcagua</a>, Argentina, the highest mountain in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Americas" title="The Americas">the Americas</a></div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mountains_in_Argentina" title="List of mountains in Argentina">List of mountains in Argentina</a></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Aconcagua" title="Aconcagua">Aconcagua</a>, 6,961 m (22,838 ft)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cerro_Bonete" title="Cerro Bonete">Cerro Bonete</a>, 6,759 m (22,175 ft)</li>
